Have a question about something specific? You can contact the edX general support team directly:



Please note: The edX support team is English speaking. While we will do our best to address your inquiry in any language, our responses will be in English.

Describe what you were doing when you encountered the issue. Include any details that will help us to troubleshoot, including error messages that you saw.

Thank You!

id=&#34;cf5b550d54ce4b9eb8b27b4d97ae25d2-problem-title&#34; aria-describedby=&#34;block-v1:ITMOx+I2CPx+3T2016+type@problem+block@cf5b550d54ce4b9eb8b27b4d97ae25d2-problem-progress&#34; tabindex=&#34;-1&#34;&gt; Bercity Underground &lt;/h3&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;problem-progress&#34; id=&#34;block-v1:ITMOx+I2CPx+3T2016+type@problem+block@cf5b550d54ce4b9eb8b27b4d97ae25d2-problem-progress&#34;&gt;&lt;/div&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;problem&#34;&gt; &lt;div&gt; &lt;span&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;tabular&#34;&gt;&lt;table border=&#34;1&#34;&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;Input &amp;#64257;le: &amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt; &lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;underground.in &lt;/td&gt; &lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;Output &amp;#64257;le: &amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt; &lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;underground.out&lt;/td&gt; &lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;Time limit: &amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt; &lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;2 seconds &lt;/td&gt; &lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;Memory limit:&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt; &lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;256 megabytes &lt;/td&gt; &lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/table&gt;&lt;/div&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;&amp;#160; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;Once upon a time, in year 2111, the Intergalactic Football Federation decided that the Bercity Football Union will conduct the Universal Football Championship in year 2118. The Mayor of Bercity now has an uneasy duty to organize such a large sport event in his city. The main problem, which he has now, is not building football &amp;#64257;elds, but preparing the infrastructure objects: transportation, hotels, food courts. You have just been asked to help him with planning of underground construction in Bercity. &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;&amp;#160; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;Football fans from certain galaxies can use only a speci&amp;#64257;c type of underground cars to move around the city. Every galaxy has its own unique type of cars, and every type of cars can move only using its own unique railway track system. No two type of cars can use the same track system. &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;&amp;#160; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;There are several stations in Bercity, and there are several bidirectional connections between certain pairs of stations. Every connection already has a particular type of the track system, so it is known which galaxy this connection is going to serve. If a station has an adjacent connection of type X, then this station should be served by a train also of type X. Of course, multiple trains may serve a single station, and a single train may serve many stations, provided it can reach them using connections of the corresponding type. &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;&amp;#160; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;It is not known yet how many car trains should be bought. To save money, it was decided that the minimum possible number of car trains will be bought, provided that all stations are fully served as described above. Given the description of the underground system, determine what is the minimum number of car trains, of each type, should be bought. &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p/&gt;&lt;p style=&#34;margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;&lt;b&gt;Input&lt;/b&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;The &amp;#64257;rst line of the input &amp;#64257;le contains three integer numbers n, m, k (1 \(\le\) n \(\le\) 10&lt;sup&gt;5&lt;/sup&gt;, 1 \(\le\) m \(\le\) 2 &amp;#8901; 10&lt;sup&gt;5&lt;/sup&gt;, 1 \(\le\) k \(\le\) 10&lt;sup&gt;5&lt;/sup&gt;), which are the number of stations, the number of connections, and the number of track system types correspondingly. &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;&amp;#160; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;The following m lines describe connections, one per line. Each connection is described by three integers: the numbers of stations it connects, and the number of the track system type which is installed in this connection. All station numbers are positive numbers not exceeding n, and the numbers of track system types are positive numbers not exceeding k. No connection goes from a station to itself. However, there can be multiple connections between the same pair of stations. &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p/&gt;&lt;p style=&#34;margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;&lt;b&gt;Output&lt;/b&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;Output k lines. The i-th line should contain the minimum possible number of car trains of type i. &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p/&gt;&lt;p style=&#34;margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;&lt;b&gt;Examples&lt;/b&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;obeylines-v&#34;&gt;&lt;div class=&#34;tabular&#34;&gt;&lt;table border=&#34;1&#34;&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;multicolumn&#34; style=&#34;white-space:nowrap; text-align:center;&#34;&gt;underground.in&lt;/div&gt; &lt;/td&gt;&lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;multicolumn&#34; style=&#34;white-space:nowrap; text-align:center;&#34;&gt;underground.out&lt;/div&gt; &lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;4 3 2 &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;1 2 1 &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;2 3 2 &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;3 4 1 &lt;/p&gt; &lt;/td&gt;&lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;2 &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;1 &lt;/p&gt; &lt;/td&gt; &lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/table&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt; &lt;p/&gt;&lt;p style=&#34;margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;&lt;b&gt;Note&lt;/b&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;In the example test, a single train of type 2 can serve all stations (2 and 3), which have a connection of type 2. However, it is impossible for a single train of type 1 to serve all stations, which have a connection of type 1, because it is impossible to reach the station 3 from the station 1 using only connections of type 1. However, two trains of type 1 are enough. &lt;/p&gt; &lt;/span&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;wrapper-problem-response&#34; tabindex=&#34;-1&#34; aria-label=&#34;Question 1&#34; role=&#34;group&#34;&gt;&lt;section id=&#34;filesubmission_cf5b550d54ce4b9eb8b27b4d97ae25d2_2_1&#34; class=&#34;filesubmission&#34;&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;grader-status file&#34;&gt; &lt;span class=&#34;incorrect&#34; id=&#34;status_cf5b550d54ce4b9eb8b27b4d97ae25d2_2_1&#34;&gt;incorrect&lt;/span&gt; &lt;p class=&#34;debug&#34;&gt;incorrect&lt;/p&gt; &lt;input type=&#34;file&#34; name=&#34;input_cf5b550d54ce4b9eb8b27b4d97ae25d2_2_1&#34; id=&#34;input_cf5b550d54ce4b9eb8b27b4d97ae25d2_2_1&#34; value=&#34;[u&#39;underground.cpp&#39;]&#34; id=&#34;1ecd41cd924f4109a20a7a42cbf2ea5a-problem-title&#34; aria-describedby=&#34;block-v1:ITMOx+I2CPx+3T2016+type@problem+block@1ecd41cd924f4109a20a7a42cbf2ea5a-problem-progress&#34; tabindex=&#34;-1&#34;&gt; Traveling Incognito &lt;/h3&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;problem-progress&#34; id=&#34;block-v1:ITMOx+I2CPx+3T2016+type@problem+block@1ecd41cd924f4109a20a7a42cbf2ea5a-problem-progress&#34;&gt;&lt;/div&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;problem&#34;&gt; &lt;div&gt; &lt;span&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;tabular&#34;&gt;&lt;table border=&#34;1&#34;&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;Input &amp;#64257;le: &amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt; &lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;travel.in &lt;/td&gt; &lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;Output &amp;#64257;le: &amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt; &lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;travel.out &lt;/td&gt; &lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;Time limit: &amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt; &lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;2 seconds &lt;/td&gt; &lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;Memory limit:&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt; &lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;256 megabytes&lt;/td&gt; &lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/table&gt;&lt;/div&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;&amp;#160; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;Scrooge McDuck recently got tired of being recognized at every street. First he was hiding in his house for several weeks, but even a billionaire needs a deep breath of fresh air. So he put on some fake mustache and decided to have an incognito journey. &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;&amp;#160; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;He planned it as follows. First, he would travel using trains exclusively. No taxis, no limousines. Second, for the &amp;#64257;rst part of the journey, he would travel using only cheap trains&amp;#160;&amp;#8211; their cost should not exceed A. And only after that, when his last traces were lost, he would regain the comfort he always liked&amp;#160;&amp;#8211; and would use trains with cost at least B. &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;&amp;#160; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;And of course, he would be paying in cash only. &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;&amp;#160; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;However, the watchful eye of the Tax Inspection was alarmed all the time. It soon became known to them that Uncle Scrooge would depart at station S and stop his journey at station T. His scheme with cheap trains followed by expensive trains remained secret no longer&amp;#160;&amp;#8211; after all, rich people, and especially rich ducks, are sometimes very predictable. And, of course, everyone knows that Scrooge McDuck would spend the minimum possible amount of money for his journey. &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;&amp;#160; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;The Tax Inspection wants to know the total cost of the incognito journey of Uncle Scrooge. Please help them! &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p/&gt;&lt;p style=&#34;margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;&lt;b&gt;Input&lt;/b&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;The &amp;#64257;rst line of the input &amp;#64257;le contains two integers N and M (1 \(\le\) N,M \(\le\) 10&lt;sup&gt;5&lt;/sup&gt;), the numbers of stations and possible trains between the stations. The second line contains two integers S and T (1 \(\le\) S, T \(\le\) 10&lt;sup&gt;5&lt;/sup&gt;). &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;&amp;#160; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;The next M lines contain descriptions of the trains. Each description consists of three integers A&lt;sub&gt;i&lt;/sub&gt;,B&lt;sub&gt;i&lt;/sub&gt;,C&lt;sub&gt;i&lt;/sub&gt; (1 \(\le\) A&lt;sub&gt;i &lt;/sub&gt; , B&lt;sub&gt;i &lt;/sub&gt; \(\le\) N, 1 \(\le\) C&lt;sub&gt;i&lt;/sub&gt; \(\le\) 10&lt;sup&gt;9&lt;/sup&gt;), the numbers of stations connected by this train, and the cost of the train. Every train can travel both from A&lt;sub&gt;i&lt;/sub&gt; to B&lt;sub&gt;i&lt;/sub&gt; and from B&lt;sub&gt;i&lt;/sub&gt; to A&lt;sub&gt;i&lt;/sub&gt;. &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;&amp;#160; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;The last line contains two integers A and B (1 \(\le\) A,B \(\le\) 10&lt;sup&gt;9&lt;/sup&gt;). &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p/&gt;&lt;p style=&#34;margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;&lt;b&gt;Output&lt;/b&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;Output the total cost of the Scrooge&amp;#8217;s journey. If there is no way to perform this journey, output &amp;#8722;1. &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;&amp;#160; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;Note that it can happen that either part of the journey (the cheap one or the expensive one) can be empty. The &amp;#64257;rst example shows precisely this kind of situation. &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p/&gt;&lt;p style=&#34;margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;&lt;b&gt;Examples&lt;/b&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;obeylines-v&#34;&gt;&lt;div class=&#34;tabular&#34;&gt;&lt;table border=&#34;1&#34;&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;multicolumn&#34; style=&#34;white-space:nowrap; text-align:center;&#34;&gt;travel.in&lt;/div&gt; &lt;/td&gt;&lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;multicolumn&#34; style=&#34;white-space:nowrap; text-align:center;&#34;&gt;travel.out&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;4 6 &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;1 4 &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;1 2 4 &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;2 4 4 &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;4 1 6 &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;1 3 7 &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;4 3 10 &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;3 2 2 &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;5 6 &lt;/p&gt; &lt;/td&gt;&lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;6 &lt;/td&gt; &lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;6 9 &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;3 2 9 &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;2 5 5 &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;1 2 1 &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;5 3 &lt;/p&gt; &lt;/td&gt;&lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;4 &lt;/td&gt; &lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/table&gt; &lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt; &lt;/span&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;wrapper-problem-response&#34; tabindex=&#34;-1&#34; aria-label=&#34;Question 1&#34; role=&#34;group&#34;&gt;&lt;section id=&#34;filesubmission_1ecd41cd924f4109a20a7a42cbf2ea5a_2_1&#34; <div class="xblock xblock-student_view xblock-student_view-vertical" data-runtime-class="LmsRuntime" data-init="VerticalStudentView" data-course-id="course-v1:ITMOx+I2CPx+3T2016" data-request-token="c46abf2cbb5511e6a3be068911e16e2e" data-runtime-version="1" data-usage-id="block-v1:ITMOx+I2CPx+3T2016+type@vertical+block@ee0863d975fd4bfcb38186ba0a7ee7bb" data-block-type="vertical"> <h3 class="unit-title">Railway Yard</h3> <div class="bookmark-button-wrapper"> <button class="btn btn-link bookmark-button " aria-pressed="false" data-bookmark-id="jasonshao8,block-v1:ITMOx+I2CPx+3T2016+type@vertical+block@ee0863d975fd4bfcb38186ba0a7ee7bb"> <span class="sr bookmark-sr">Click to add</span> <span class="bookmark-text">Bookmark this page</span> </button> </div> <div class="vert-mod"> <div class="vert vert-0" data-id="block-v1:ITMOx+I2CPx+3T2016+type@problem+block@34253226b934466e81ab10a5d9eed8e4"> <div class="xblock xblock-student_view xblock-student_view-problem xmodule_display xmodule_CapaModule" data-runtime-class="LmsRuntime" data-init="XBlockToXModuleShim" data-block-type="problem" data-request-token="c46abf2cbb5511e6a3be068911e16e2e" data-runtime-version="1" data-usage-id="block-v1:ITMOx+I2CPx+3T2016+type@problem+block@34253226b934466e81ab10a5d9eed8e4" data-type="Problem" data-course-id="course-v1:ITMOx+I2CPx+3T2016"> <script type="json/xblock-args" class="xblock-json-init-args"> {"xmodule-type": "Problem"} </script> <div id="problem_34253226b934466e81ab10a5d9eed8e4" class="problems-wrapper" role="group" aria-labelledby="34253226b934466e81ab10a5d9eed8e4-problem-title" data-problem-id="block-v1:ITMOx+I2CPx+3T2016+type@problem+block@34253226b934466e81ab10a5d9eed8e4" data-url="/courses/course-v1:ITMOx+I2CPx+3T2016/xblock/block-v1:ITMOx+I2CPx+3T2016+type@problem+block@34253226b934466e81ab10a5d9eed8e4/handler/xmodule_handler" data-problem-score="0.0" data-problem-total-possible="4.0" data-attempts-used="0" data-content=" &lt;h3 class=&#34;hd hd-2 problem-header&#34; id=&#34;34253226b934466e81ab10a5d9eed8e4-problem-title&#34; aria-describedby=&#34;block-v1:ITMOx+I2CPx+3T2016+type@problem+block@34253226b934466e81ab10a5d9eed8e4-problem-progress&#34; tabindex=&#34;-1&#34;&gt; Railway Yard &lt;/h3&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;problem-progress&#34; id=&#34;block-v1:ITMOx+I2CPx+3T2016+type@problem+block@34253226b934466e81ab10a5d9eed8e4-problem-progress&#34;&gt;&lt;/div&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;problem&#34;&gt; &lt;div&gt; &lt;span&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;tabular&#34;&gt;&lt;table border=&#34;1&#34;&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;Input &amp;#64257;le: &amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt; &lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;railway.in &lt;/td&gt; &lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;Output &amp;#64257;le: &amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt; &lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;railway.out &lt;/td&gt; &lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;Time limit: &amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt; &lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;2 seconds &lt;/td&gt; &lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;Memory limit:&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt; &lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;256 megabytes&lt;/td&gt; &lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/table&gt;&lt;/div&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;&amp;#160; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;There are N boxcars standing at the railway yard. All these boxcars have the same length, but they contain various goods, so they have di&amp;#64256;erent masses. In order to form a train, these boxcars should be rearranged in the increasing order of their masses&amp;#160;&amp;#8211; only after that the train can be formed from these boxcars and will be allowed to proceed to its &amp;#64257;nal destination. &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;&amp;#160; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;To achieve this aim, so called &lt;em&gt;shunting locomotives&lt;/em&gt; are typically used. But this particular yard is equipped with an experimental sorting device. It is supposed that using this device will signi&amp;#64257;cantly reduce the time needed to form the train. &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;&amp;#160; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;This device has a length which slightly exceeds the length of two boxcars. It can be located above two consecutive boxcars, lift them to the air, swap them and put them back. However, the maximum load for this device is limited: the total mass of the boxcars engaged in this operation must not exceed M. &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;&amp;#160; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;Your task is to write a program which determines whether it is possible to sort the given boxcars in the increasing order of their masses using this device. &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p/&gt;&lt;p style=&#34;margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;&lt;b&gt;Input&lt;/b&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;The &amp;#64257;rst line of the input &amp;#64257;le contains two numbers: the number of boxcars N&amp;#160;(2 \(\le\) N \(\le\) 100&lt;span style=&#34;margin-left:0.3em&#34; class=&#34;thinspace&#34;/&gt;000) and the maximum load of the experimental swapping device&amp;#160;M (1 \(\le\) M \(\le\) 10&lt;sup&gt;9&lt;/sup&gt;). &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;&amp;#160; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;The second line of the input &amp;#64257;le contains the masses of the boxcars M&lt;sub&gt;1&lt;/sub&gt;,&amp;#8230;,M&lt;sub&gt;N&lt;/sub&gt;. These masses satisfy 1 \(\le\) M&lt;sub&gt;i &lt;/sub&gt; \(\le\) 10&lt;sup&gt;9 &lt;/sup&gt; , what is more, the masses are pairwise di&amp;#64256;erent. The masses are listed in the order the boxcars are currently standing. &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p/&gt;&lt;p style=&#34;margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;&lt;b&gt;Output&lt;/b&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;Output &amp;#8220;Yes&amp;#8221; if it is possible to order the boxcars using the experimental swapping device. If it is impossible, output &amp;#8220;No&amp;#8221;. &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p/&gt;&lt;p style=&#34;margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;&lt;b&gt;Examples&lt;/b&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;obeylines-v&#34;&gt;&lt;div class=&#34;tabular&#34;&gt;&lt;table border=&#34;1&#34;&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;multicolumn&#34; style=&#34;white-space:nowrap; text-align:center;&#34;&gt;railway.in&lt;/div&gt; &lt;/td&gt;&lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;multicolumn&#34; style=&#34;white-space:nowrap; text-align:center;&#34;&gt;railway.out&lt;/div&gt; &lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;4 10 &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;5 6 3 4 &lt;/p&gt; &lt;/td&gt;&lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;Yes &lt;/td&gt; &lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;4 9 &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;5 6 3 4 &lt;/p&gt; &lt;/td&gt;&lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;No &lt;/td&gt; &lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/table&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt; &lt;/span&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;wrapper-problem-response&#34; tabindex=&#34;-1&#34; aria-label=&#34;Question 1&#34; role=&#34;group&#34;&gt;&lt;section id=&#34;filesubmission_34253226b934466e81ab10a5d9eed8e4_2_1&#34; class=&#34;filesubmission&#34;&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;grader-status file&#34;&gt; &lt;span class=&#34;unanswered&#34; id=&#34;status_34253226b934466e81ab10a5d9eed8e4_2_1&#34;&gt;unanswered&lt;/span&gt; &lt;p class=&#34;debug&#34;&gt;unsubmitted&lt;/p&gt; &lt;input type=&#34;file&#34; <div class="xblock xblock-student_view xblock-student_view-vertical" data-runtime-class="LmsRuntime" data-init="VerticalStudentView" data-course-id="course-v1:ITMOx+I2CPx+3T2016" data-request-token="c46abf2cbb5511e6a3be068911e16e2e" data-runtime-version="1" data-usage-id="block-v1:ITMOx+I2CPx+3T2016+type@vertical+block@2a1e943820054bebb26f0c5d83985a29" data-block-type="vertical"> <h3 class="unit-title">Moscow 2042</h3> <div class="bookmark-button-wrapper"> <button class="btn btn-link bookmark-button " aria-pressed="false" data-bookmark-id="jasonshao8,block-v1:ITMOx+I2CPx+3T2016+type@vertical+block@2a1e943820054bebb26f0c5d83985a29"> <span class="sr bookmark-sr">Click to add</span> <span class="bookmark-text">Bookmark this page</span> </button> </div> <div class="vert-mod"> <div class="vert vert-0" data-id="block-v1:ITMOx+I2CPx+3T2016+type@problem+block@d0b2ba9cf50d4abbb0f7d60351f64406"> <div class="xblock xblock-student_view xblock-student_view-problem xmodule_display xmodule_CapaModule" data-runtime-class="LmsRuntime" data-init="XBlockToXModuleShim" data-block-type="problem" data-request-token="c46abf2cbb5511e6a3be068911e16e2e" data-runtime-version="1" data-usage-id="block-v1:ITMOx+I2CPx+3T2016+type@problem+block@d0b2ba9cf50d4abbb0f7d60351f64406" data-type="Problem" data-course-id="course-v1:ITMOx+I2CPx+3T2016"> <script type="json/xblock-args" class="xblock-json-init-args"> {"xmodule-type": "Problem"} </script> <div id="problem_d0b2ba9cf50d4abbb0f7d60351f64406" class="problems-wrapper" role="group" aria-labelledby="d0b2ba9cf50d4abbb0f7d60351f64406-problem-title" data-problem-id="block-v1:ITMOx+I2CPx+3T2016+type@problem+block@d0b2ba9cf50d4abbb0f7d60351f64406" data-url="/courses/course-v1:ITMOx+I2CPx+3T2016/xblock/block-v1:ITMOx+I2CPx+3T2016+type@problem+block@d0b2ba9cf50d4abbb0f7d60351f64406/handler/xmodule_handler" data-problem-score="0.0" data-problem-total-possible="4.0" data-attempts-used="0" data-content=" &lt;h3 class=&#34;hd hd-2 problem-header&#34; id=&#34;d0b2ba9cf50d4abbb0f7d60351f64406-problem-title&#34; aria-describedby=&#34;block-v1:ITMOx+I2CPx+3T2016+type@problem+block@d0b2ba9cf50d4abbb0f7d60351f64406-problem-progress&#34; tabindex=&#34;-1&#34;&gt; Moscow 2042 &lt;/h3&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;problem-progress&#34; id=&#34;block-v1:ITMOx+I2CPx+3T2016+type@problem+block@d0b2ba9cf50d4abbb0f7d60351f64406-problem-progress&#34;&gt;&lt;/div&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;problem&#34;&gt; &lt;div&gt; &lt;span&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;tabular&#34;&gt;&lt;table border=&#34;1&#34;&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;Input &amp;#64257;le: &amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt; &lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;moscow.in &lt;/td&gt; &lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;Output &amp;#64257;le: &amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt; &lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;moscow.out &lt;/td&gt; &lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;Time limit: &amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt; &lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;2 seconds &lt;/td&gt; &lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;Memory limit:&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt; &lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;256 megabytes&lt;/td&gt; &lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/table&gt;&lt;/div&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;&amp;#160; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;By year 2042, the Government of Moscow has &amp;#64257;nished yet another large-scale project, which resulted in the increase of the number of circular highways up to N. Now, a driver has exponentially more ways to slug through tra&amp;#64259;c jams while moving from one point of the city to another one. &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;&amp;#160; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;The &amp;#8220;Giggle&amp;#8221; company plans to support a new feature in its &amp;#8220;Giggle Maps&amp;#8221; product: building of an optimal path from one junction to another one. In the internal representation of this program, the Moscow map is a set of M radial and N circular highways. &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;&amp;#160; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;In the &amp;#8220;Giggle&amp;#8221;&amp;#8217;s mathematical model, all circular highways are circles with centers located exactly at the center of the Red Square and radii of R&lt;sub&gt;1&lt;/sub&gt;,R&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;,&amp;#8230;R&lt;sub&gt;N&lt;/sub&gt;. All radial highways are segments with one of the endpoints exactly at the center of the Red Square, and another endpoint is at the circular highway having a maximum radius. If one stands at the center of the Red Square and looks straight to east, then to look along the j-th radial highway, one should turn counter-clockwise by &amp;#945;&lt;sub&gt;j&lt;/sub&gt; degrees. &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;&amp;#160; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;All radial highways are bidirectional. Some circular highways are bidirectional too, but others are unidirectional, and may be oriented either clockwise or counter-clockwise. &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;&amp;#160; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;Help &amp;#8220;Giggle&amp;#8221; to &amp;#64257;nd the shortest path from the junction where the (i&lt;sub&gt;s&lt;/sub&gt;)-th circular and (j&lt;sub&gt;s&lt;/sub&gt;)-th radial highways intersect to the junction where the (i&lt;sub&gt;t&lt;/sub&gt;)-th circular and (j&lt;sub&gt;t&lt;/sub&gt;)-th radial highways intersect. Note that one is not allowed to drive through the Red Square. &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p/&gt;&lt;p style=&#34;margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;&lt;b&gt;Input&lt;/b&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;The &amp;#64257;rst line of the input &amp;#64257;le contains two integers N and M (1 \(\le\) N,M \(\le\) 100&lt;span style=&#34;margin-left:0.3em&#34; class=&#34;thinspace&#34;/&gt;000). &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;&amp;#160; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;The following N lines describe the circular highways. Every such highway is described by its radius R&lt;sub&gt;i&lt;/sub&gt; (1 \(\le\) R&lt;sub&gt;i &lt;/sub&gt; \(\le\) 10&lt;sup&gt;6 &lt;/sup&gt; ) and a number D&lt;sub&gt;i&lt;/sub&gt;. If D&lt;sub&gt;i&lt;/sub&gt; = 0, then this highway is bidirectional, if D&lt;sub&gt;i&lt;/sub&gt; = 1, then you can drive counter-clockwise only (to the direction of radial highway angle increase), if D&lt;sub&gt;i&lt;/sub&gt; = &amp;#8722;1, then you can drive clockwise only. &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;&amp;#160; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;The following M lines describe the radial highways. Every such highway is described by a single integer A&lt;sub&gt;j&lt;/sub&gt;, such that &amp;#945;&lt;sub&gt;j &lt;/sub&gt; = A&lt;sub&gt;j &lt;/sub&gt; &amp;#8725;10&lt;sup&gt;6&lt;/sup&gt; (0 \(\le\) A&lt;sub&gt;j&lt;/sub&gt; &amp;lt; 360 &amp;#8901; 10&lt;sup&gt;6&lt;/sup&gt;). &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;&amp;#160; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;Two lines follow. The &amp;#64257;rst of them contains the numbers i&lt;sub&gt;s&lt;/sub&gt; and j&lt;sub&gt;s&lt;/sub&gt;, the second one the numbers i&lt;sub&gt;t&lt;/sub&gt; and j&lt;sub&gt;t&lt;/sub&gt;. It holds that 1 \(\le\) i&lt;sub&gt;s &lt;/sub&gt; , i&lt;sub&gt;t &lt;/sub&gt; \(\le\) N, and 1 \(\le\) j&lt;sub&gt;s&lt;/sub&gt;,j&lt;sub&gt;t&lt;/sub&gt; \(\le\) M. &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p/&gt;&lt;p style=&#34;margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;&lt;b&gt;Output&lt;/b&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;Output a single number: the minimal distance, which one has to drive to get from the junction of the (i&lt;sub&gt;s&lt;/sub&gt;)-th circular and (j&lt;sub&gt;s&lt;/sub&gt;)-th radial highways to the junction of the (i&lt;sub&gt;t&lt;/sub&gt;)-th circular and (j&lt;sub&gt;t&lt;/sub&gt;)-th radial highways. Your answer should di&amp;#64256;er from the right one by at most 10&lt;sup&gt;&amp;#8722;4&lt;/sup&gt;. &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p/&gt;&lt;p style=&#34;margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;&lt;b&gt;Example&lt;/b&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;tabular&#34;&gt;&lt;table border=&#34;1&#34;&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;&lt;div class=&#34;obeylines-v&#34;&gt;&lt;div class=&#34;tabular&#34;&gt;&lt;table border=&#34;1&#34;&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;&lt;div class=&#34;multicolumn&#34; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;7 1 &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;8 -1 &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;180000000 &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;270000000 &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;3 1 &lt;/p&gt; id=&#34;3cc65e74c7a140b583fb98e30dfcf9d7-problem-title&#34; aria-describedby=&#34;block-v1:ITMOx+I2CPx+3T2016+type@problem+block@3cc65e74c7a140b583fb98e30dfcf9d7-problem-progress&#34; tabindex=&#34;-1&#34;&gt; Expensive Trees &lt;/h3&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;problem-progress&#34; id=&#34;block-v1:ITMOx+I2CPx+3T2016+type@problem+block@3cc65e74c7a140b583fb98e30dfcf9d7-problem-progress&#34;&gt;&lt;/div&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;problem&#34;&gt; &lt;div&gt; &lt;span&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;tabular&#34;&gt;&lt;table border=&#34;1&#34;&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;Input &amp;#64257;le: &amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt; &lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;trees.in &lt;/td&gt; &lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;Output &amp;#64257;le: &amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt; &lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;trees.out &lt;/td&gt; &lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;Time limit: &amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt; &lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;2 seconds &lt;/td&gt; &lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;Memory limit:&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt; &lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;256 megabytes&lt;/td&gt; &lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/table&gt;&lt;/div&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;&amp;#160; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;Following his uncle Scrooge McDuck, Donald Duck decided to start making money. Various things are being sold for money, but Donald Duck decided to sell rooted trees. &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;&amp;#160; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;Everybody knows that a rooted tree is a tree with a certain vertex di&amp;#64256;erent from every other vertex and called a &lt;em&gt;root&lt;/em&gt;. Everybody making serious businesses also knows that the price of a rooted tree is the sum of depths of its leaves. The root of the tree has the depth 0, and the depth of any other vertex is one plus the depth of its parent. Donald Duck was quite fast at learning how to compute the price of a rooted tree. But he still has problems constructing expensive trees. &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;&amp;#160; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;Donald has N vertices and N &amp;#8722; 1 edges. He can construct one or more trees from them, and subsequently sell them. Help him and &amp;#64257;nd the maximum total price for the trees he can construct. &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p/&gt;&lt;p style=&#34;margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;&lt;b&gt;Input&lt;/b&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;The &amp;#64257;rst line of the input &amp;#64257;le contains a single integer number N (1 \(\le\) N \(\le\) 8&lt;span style=&#34;margin-left:0.3em&#34; class=&#34;thinspace&#34;/&gt;589&lt;span style=&#34;margin-left:0.3em&#34; class=&#34;thinspace&#34;/&gt;934&lt;span style=&#34;margin-left:0.3em&#34; class=&#34;thinspace&#34;/&gt;591), the number of vertices Donald Duck has. &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p/&gt;&lt;p style=&#34;margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;&lt;b&gt;Output&lt;/b&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;Print a single number, the maximum total price of the constructed trees. &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p/&gt;&lt;p style=&#34;margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;&lt;b&gt;Examples&lt;/b&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;obeylines-v&#34;&gt;&lt;div class=&#34;tabular&#34;&gt;&lt;table border=&#34;1&#34;&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;multicolumn&#34; style=&#34;white-space:nowrap; text-align:center;&#34;&gt;trees.in&lt;/div&gt; &lt;/td&gt;&lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;multicolumn&#34; style=&#34;white-space:nowrap; text-align:center;&#34;&gt;trees.out&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;3&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;2 &lt;/td&gt; &lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/table&gt; &lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt; &lt;p/&gt;&lt;p style=&#34;margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;&lt;b&gt;Note&lt;/b&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;In this example, a single tree is enough. Let the root of the tree be the vertex 1, then it brings the maximum pro&amp;#64257;t to make edges 1 &amp;#8594; 2 and 1 &amp;#8594; 3. The price of the tree would be the sum of the depths of vertices 2 and 3, that is, 1 + 1 = 2. &lt;/p&gt; &lt;/span&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;wrapper-problem-response&#34; tabindex=&#34;-1&#34; aria-label=&#34;Question 1&#34; role=&#34;group&#34;&gt;&lt;section id=&#34;filesubmission_3cc65e74c7a140b583fb98e30dfcf9d7_2_1&#34; class=&#34;filesubmission&#34;&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;grader-status file&#34;&gt; &lt;span class=&#34;correct&#34; id=&#34;status_3cc65e74c7a140b583fb98e30dfcf9d7_2_1&#34;&gt;correct&lt;/span&gt; &lt;p class=&#34;debug&#34;&gt;correct&lt;/p&gt; &lt;input type=&#34;file&#34; name=&#34;input_3cc65e74c7a140b583fb98e30dfcf9d7_2_1&#34; &lt;/div&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;message&#34; tabindex=&#34;-1&#34;&gt;Accepted&lt;/div&gt; &lt;/section&gt;&lt;/div&gt; &lt;/div&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;action&#34;&gt; &lt;input type=&#34;hidden&#34; Sherlocked &lt;/h3&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;problem-progress&#34; id=&#34;block-v1:ITMOx+I2CPx+3T2016+type@problem+block@e5b74be282b840f6ad53ccd44da997ae-problem-progress&#34;&gt;&lt;/div&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;problem&#34;&gt; &lt;div&gt; &lt;span&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;tabular&#34;&gt;&lt;table border=&#34;1&#34;&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;Input &amp;#64257;le: &amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt; &lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;sherlocked.in &lt;/td&gt; &lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;Output &amp;#64257;le: &amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt; &lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;sherlocked.out&lt;/td&gt; &lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;Time limit: &amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt; &lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;2 seconds &lt;/td&gt; &lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;Memory limit:&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt; &lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;256 megabytes &lt;/td&gt; &lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/table&gt;&lt;/div&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;&amp;#160; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;Sherlock Holmes has recently received a locked mobile phone of Irene Adler. The lockscreen contained a short text, which said that this phone contains private SSH keys of Prof.&amp;#160;James Moriarty, and a map showing the current location of Irene herself. But in order to unlock the phone, Sherlock should solve a puzzle which was located on the same lockscreen. He has only one attempt, the text said, and if it is unsuccessful, the phone would heat itself and blow up. &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;&amp;#160; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;The puzzle is a N &amp;#215; M table, where each cell contains an integer number. While searching for possible clues, Sherlock turned the phone over and saw a snake crawling up a ladder, which was graved at the rear surface of the phone. &amp;#8220;It is obvious,&amp;#8221; said Sherlock immediately, &amp;#8220;she wants me to &amp;#64257;nd the longest chain of consecutive numbers in this table.&amp;#8221; In a couple of seconds, the phone was unlocked, and the story began&amp;#8230; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;&amp;#160; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;Sherlock was so clever that he could perform &amp;#1012;(N&lt;sup&gt;2&lt;/sup&gt; &amp;#8901; M&lt;sup&gt;2&lt;/sup&gt;) operations per second in his mind. Could you? Then &amp;#64257;nd the length of the longest chain of consecutive numbers in the given table, just as Sherlock did. A &lt;em&gt;chain&lt;/em&gt; is a sequence of table cells, such that any two consecutive cells have a common side. &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p/&gt;&lt;p style=&#34;margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;&lt;b&gt;Input&lt;/b&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;The &amp;#64257;rst line of the input &amp;#64257;le contains numbers N and M (1 \(\le\) N,M \(\le\) 1000). The next N lines contain M numbers each, the values of the table A&lt;sub&gt;i,j&lt;/sub&gt; (1 \(\le\) A&lt;sub&gt;i,j&lt;/sub&gt; \(\le\) 10 &amp;#215; N &amp;#215; M). &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p/&gt;&lt;p style=&#34;margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;&lt;b&gt;Output&lt;/b&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;Output the length of the longest chain of consecutive numbers. &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p/&gt;&lt;p style=&#34;margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;&lt;b&gt;Examples&lt;/b&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;obeylines-v&#34;&gt;&lt;div class=&#34;tabular&#34;&gt;&lt;table border=&#34;1&#34;&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;multicolumn&#34; id=&#34;9f2126be5d904730924a2f6b9656055f-problem-title&#34; aria-describedby=&#34;block-v1:ITMOx+I2CPx+3T2016+type@problem+block@9f2126be5d904730924a2f6b9656055f-problem-progress&#34; tabindex=&#34;-1&#34;&gt; Bytelandian Cars &lt;/h3&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;problem-progress&#34; id=&#34;block-v1:ITMOx+I2CPx+3T2016+type@problem+block@9f2126be5d904730924a2f6b9656055f-problem-progress&#34;&gt;&lt;/div&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;problem&#34;&gt; &lt;div&gt; &lt;span&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;tabular&#34;&gt;&lt;table border=&#34;1&#34;&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;Input &amp;#64257;le: &amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt; &lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;cars.in &lt;/td&gt; &lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;Output &amp;#64257;le: &amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt; &lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;cars.out &lt;/td&gt; &lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;Time limit: &amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt; &lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;2 seconds &lt;/td&gt; &lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;Memory limit:&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt; &lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;256 megabytes&lt;/td&gt; &lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/table&gt;&lt;/div&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;&amp;#160; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;Byteland is a country which is very famous for menufacturing various car models. Although some of these models are withdrawn from the market, there are more and more new models every year. Every model is characterized by many various parameters, but price is among the most important ones. &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;&amp;#160; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;The football players, which play for the local football team &amp;#8220;The Target Hitting Bug&amp;#8221; are quite strange people. When one of them buys a car, he looks at the price for the &amp;#64257;rst turn. A car is &amp;#8220;too expensive&amp;#8221;, if its price is greater than the mean price of all models currently on market. Similarly, a car is &amp;#8220;too cheap&amp;#8221;, if its price is smaller than the mean price of all models currently on market. All other cars immediately draw attention of local football players. &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;&amp;#160; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;As Byteland car manufacturers conduct marketing researches from time to time, they often want to know, how much models will be of any interest from the point of view of local football players. You were asked to write a common uni&amp;#64257;ed service to help all of them. &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p/&gt;&lt;p style=&#34;margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;&lt;b&gt;Input&lt;/b&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;The &amp;#64257;rst line of the input &amp;#64257;le contains the number of queries N (2 \(\le\) N \(\le\) 2 &amp;#183; 10&lt;sup&gt;5&lt;/sup&gt;). The following N lines contain queries. A query can have one of the following types: &lt;/p&gt; &lt;ul class=&#34;itemize1&#34;&gt; &lt;li class=&#34;itemize&#34;&gt;+&amp;#160;K: a new model, which has the price K, is started to be manufactured. 0 \(\le\) K \(\le\) 10&lt;sup&gt;13&lt;/sup&gt;, K is an integer. &lt;/li&gt; &lt;li class=&#34;itemize&#34;&gt;&amp;#8722;: the most dated model&amp;#160;&amp;#8211; that is, the model, which is currently manufactured, but is the oldest one among all such models&amp;#160;&amp;#8211; is withdrawn from the market. It is guaranteed that when such query arrives, there is at least one model currently manufactured. &lt;/li&gt; &lt;li class=&#34;itemize&#34;&gt;?: the question, how many models there are, whose price is equal to the mean price of all models currently manufactured? It is guaranteed that when such query arrives, there is at least one model currently manufactured.&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;Initially, there are no models being manufactured. &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p/&gt;&lt;p style=&#34;margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;&lt;b&gt;Output&lt;/b&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;For every &amp;#8220;?&amp;#8221; query, print the answer to the question, in the order of appearance, one per line. &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p/&gt;&lt;p style=&#34;margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;&lt;b&gt;Example&lt;/b&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;obeylines-v&#34;&gt;&lt;div class=&#34;tabular&#34;&gt;&lt;table border=&#34;1&#34;&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;multicolumn&#34; style=&#34;white-space:nowrap; text-align:center;&#34;&gt;cars.in&lt;/div&gt; &lt;/td&gt;&lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;multicolumn&#34; style=&#34;white-space:nowrap; text-align:center;&#34;&gt;cars.out&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;10 &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;+ 1 &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;+ 4 &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;+ 3 &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;+ 4 &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;? &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;- &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;- &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;? &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;- &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;? &lt;/p&gt; &lt;/td&gt;&lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;1 &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; <div class="xblock xblock-student_view xblock-student_view-vertical" data-runtime-class="LmsRuntime" data-init="VerticalStudentView" data-course-id="course-v1:ITMOx+I2CPx+3T2016" data-request-token="c46abf2cbb5511e6a3be068911e16e2e" data-runtime-version="1" data-usage-id="block-v1:ITMOx+I2CPx+3T2016+type@vertical+block@0800aee7d3da4c989c1f7b7814424ddf" data-block-type="vertical"> <h3 class="unit-title">Hakuna Matata Sort</h3> <div class="bookmark-button-wrapper"> <button class="btn btn-link bookmark-button " aria-pressed="false" data-bookmark-id="jasonshao8,block-v1:ITMOx+I2CPx+3T2016+type@vertical+block@0800aee7d3da4c989c1f7b7814424ddf"> <span class="sr bookmark-sr">Click to add</span> <span class="bookmark-text">Bookmark this page</span> </button> </div> <div class="vert-mod"> <div class="vert vert-0" data-id="block-v1:ITMOx+I2CPx+3T2016+type@problem+block@d552950e6a894bdeb05bf2cb85451d8b"> <div class="xblock xblock-student_view xblock-student_view-problem xmodule_display xmodule_CapaModule" data-runtime-class="LmsRuntime" data-init="XBlockToXModuleShim" data-block-type="problem" data-request-token="c46abf2cbb5511e6a3be068911e16e2e" data-runtime-version="1" data-usage-id="block-v1:ITMOx+I2CPx+3T2016+type@problem+block@d552950e6a894bdeb05bf2cb85451d8b" data-type="Problem" data-course-id="course-v1:ITMOx+I2CPx+3T2016"> <script type="json/xblock-args" class="xblock-json-init-args"> {"xmodule-type": "Problem"} </script> <div id="problem_d552950e6a894bdeb05bf2cb85451d8b" class="problems-wrapper" role="group" aria-labelledby="d552950e6a894bdeb05bf2cb85451d8b-problem-title" data-problem-id="block-v1:ITMOx+I2CPx+3T2016+type@problem+block@d552950e6a894bdeb05bf2cb85451d8b" data-url="/courses/course-v1:ITMOx+I2CPx+3T2016/xblock/block-v1:ITMOx+I2CPx+3T2016+type@problem+block@d552950e6a894bdeb05bf2cb85451d8b/handler/xmodule_handler" data-problem-score="0.0" data-problem-total-possible="4.0" data-attempts-used="0" data-content=" &lt;h3 class=&#34;hd hd-2 problem-header&#34; id=&#34;d552950e6a894bdeb05bf2cb85451d8b-problem-title&#34; aria-describedby=&#34;block-v1:ITMOx+I2CPx+3T2016+type@problem+block@d552950e6a894bdeb05bf2cb85451d8b-problem-progress&#34; tabindex=&#34;-1&#34;&gt; Hakuna Matata Sort &lt;/h3&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;problem-progress&#34; id=&#34;block-v1:ITMOx+I2CPx+3T2016+type@problem+block@d552950e6a894bdeb05bf2cb85451d8b-problem-progress&#34;&gt;&lt;/div&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;problem&#34;&gt; &lt;div&gt; &lt;span&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;tabular&#34;&gt;&lt;table border=&#34;1&#34;&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;Input &amp;#64257;le: &amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt; &lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;sort.in &lt;/td&gt; &lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;Output &amp;#64257;le: &amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt; &lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;sort.out &lt;/td&gt; &lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;Time limit: &amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt; &lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;2 seconds &lt;/td&gt; &lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;Memory limit:&amp;#160;&lt;/td&gt; &lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;256 megabytes&lt;/td&gt; &lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/table&gt;&lt;/div&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;&amp;#160; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;After a joyful walk in an African valley, Timon and Pumbaa decided to have a lunch. For this purpose, they took N beetles from under a stone and put them in a row onto a nearby log. These beetles have di&amp;#64256;erent integer masses from 1 to N. To make the lunch funnier, Pumbaa suggested to eat these beetles in the increasing order of their masses. &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;&amp;#160; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;To sort beetles in the increasing order of their masses, Timon and Pumbaa use the Hakuna Matata Sort. It works as follows: the friends choose two beetles, which di&amp;#64256;er in mass by at most one, and swap them. For instance, if Pumbaa chose a beetle with mass 2, then Timon can choose one with either mass 1 or 3. They used this sorting algorithm previously many times, so they know it works. &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;&amp;#160; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;Meanwhile, Zazu was watching this process with full attention. He saw something like this for the &amp;#64257;rst time. He is interested, how it is possible to sort beetles in such a way. Help him an write a program, which, given the initial locations of beetles, prints the sequence of actions which sorts the beetles in the increasing order of their masses. &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p/&gt;&lt;p style=&#34;margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;&lt;b&gt;Input&lt;/b&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;The &amp;#64257;rst line of the input &amp;#64257;le contains the integer number N (1 \(\le\) N \(\le\) 100), the number of beetles. The next line contains N di&amp;#64256;erent integers M&lt;sub&gt;i&lt;/sub&gt; (1 \(\le\) M&lt;sub&gt;i&lt;/sub&gt; \(\le\) N), such that M&lt;sub&gt;i&lt;/sub&gt; is the mass of a beetle at position i. &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p/&gt;&lt;p style=&#34;margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;&lt;b&gt;Output&lt;/b&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;In the &amp;#64257;rst line print the number of operations T in a possible run of the Hakuna Matata Sort. In the following T lines print the actions. If the s-th of these lines contains two numbers i and j, it means that at the s-th step Pumbaa took a beetle at position i, and Timon took a beetle at position j, then they swapped these beetles. &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;&amp;#160; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;Your sorting run should consist of at most 50000 actions. &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p/&gt;&lt;p style=&#34;margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;&lt;b&gt;Example&lt;/b&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;obeylines-v&#34;&gt;&lt;div class=&#34;tabular&#34;&gt;&lt;table border=&#34;1&#34;&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;multicolumn&#34; style=&#34;white-space:nowrap; text-align:center;&#34;&gt;sort.in&lt;/div&gt; &lt;/td&gt;&lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;multicolumn&#34; style=&#34;white-space:nowrap; text-align:center;&#34;&gt;sort.out&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;3 &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;2 3 1 &lt;/p&gt; &lt;/td&gt;&lt;td style=&#34;vertical-align:top&#34;&gt;2 &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;1 3 &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p style=&#34;padding-top:0em; margin-top:0em; margin-bottom:0em;&#34;&gt;2 3 &lt;/p&gt; &lt;/td&gt; &lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/table&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/div&gt; &lt;/span&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;wrapper-problem-response&#34; tabindex=&#34;-1&#34; aria-label=&#34;Question 1&#34; role=&#34;group&#34;&gt;&lt;section id=&#34;filesubmission_d552950e6a894bdeb05bf2cb85451d8b_2_1&#34; class=&#34;filesubmission&#34;&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;grader-status file&#34;&gt; &lt;span class=&#34;unanswered&#34; id=&#34;status_d552950e6a894bdeb05bf2cb85451d8b_2_1&#34;&gt;unanswered&lt;/span&gt; &lt;p class=&#34;debug&#34;&gt;unsubmitted&lt;/p&gt; &lt;input type=&#34;file&#34; Hakuna Matata Sort

Hakuna Matata Sort

4.0 points possible (graded)
Input le:   sort.in
Output le:   sort.out
Time limit:   2 seconds
Memory limit:  256 megabytes

 

After a joyful walk in an African valley, Timon and Pumbaa decided to have a lunch. For this purpose, they took N beetles from under a stone and put them in a row onto a nearby log. These beetles have dierent integer masses from 1 to N. To make the lunch funnier, Pumbaa suggested to eat these beetles in the increasing order of their masses.

 

To sort beetles in the increasing order of their masses, Timon and Pumbaa use the Hakuna Matata Sort. It works as follows: the friends choose two beetles, which dier in mass by at most one, and swap them. For instance, if Pumbaa chose a beetle with mass 2, then Timon can choose one with either mass 1 or 3. They used this sorting algorithm previously many times, so they know it works.

 

Meanwhile, Zazu was watching this process with full attention. He saw something like this for the rst time. He is interested, how it is possible to sort beetles in such a way. Help him an write a program, which, given the initial locations of beetles, prints the sequence of actions which sorts the beetles in the increasing order of their masses.

Input

The rst line of the input le contains the integer number N (1 N 100), the number of beetles. The next line contains N dierent integers Mi (1 Mi N), such that Mi is the mass of a beetle at position i.

Output

In the rst line print the number of operations T in a possible run of the Hakuna Matata Sort. In the following T lines print the actions. If the s-th of these lines contains two numbers i and j, it means that at the s-th step Pumbaa took a beetle at position i, and Timon took a beetle at position j, then they swapped these beetles.

 

Your sorting run should consist of at most 50000 actions.

Example

sort.in
sort.out
3

2 3 1

2

1 3

2 3
